"To solve this problem, we need to determine the total area that the cow can graze and then calculate how many days it will take for the cow to graze that entire area at a rate of 10 square feet per day.\n\nLet's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the radius of the grazing area:**\n   - The cow is tethered with a 14-foot long rope, so the radius of the grazing area is 14 feet.\n\n2. **Calculate the area of the circle:**\n   - The formula for the area of a circle is \\( \\text{Area} = \\pi \\times \\text{radius}^2 \\).\n   - Substituting the radius, we get:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Area} = \\pi \\times 14^2 = \\pi \\times 196\n     \\]\n   - Using the approximation \\( \\pi \\approx 3.14 \\), we calculate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Area} \\approx 3.14 \\times 196 = 615.44 \\text{ square feet}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Determine the number of days to graze the entire area:**\n   - The cow grazes 10 square feet per day.\n   - To find the number of days required, divide the total area by the grazing rate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Days} = \\frac{615.44}{10} \\approx 61.544\n     \\]\n\n4. **Round to the nearest whole number:**\n   - Since the cow cannot graze a fraction of a day, we round 61.544 to the nearest whole number, which is 62 days.\n\nHowever, since the answer choices provided are in whole numbers and the closest option to 62 is 61, we choose:\n\n**Answer: B) 61 days**"
'To solve this problem, we need to follow the steps outlined in the hint and calculate the cost price (CP) first, then determine the profit or loss percentage when the book is sold for Rs. 25.75.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Determine the Cost Price (CP):**\n   - We know the book was sold for Rs. 27.50 with a profit of 10%.\n   - The formula to calculate the cost price when the selling price and profit percentage are known is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{CP} = \\frac{\\text{Selling Price}}{1 + \\text{Profit Percentage}}\n     \\]\n   - Here, the selling price is Rs. 27.50 and the profit percentage is 10% (or 0.10 in decimal form).\n   - Substitute the values into the formula:\n     \\[\n     \\text{CP} = \\frac{27.50}{1 + 0.10} = \\frac{27.50}{1.10} = 25.00\n     \\]\n   - So, the cost price of the book is Rs. 25.00.\n\n2. **Calculate the Profit or Loss when sold for Rs. 25.75:**\n   - New selling price = Rs. 25.75\n   - Cost price = Rs. 25.00\n   - Profit or Loss = Selling Price - Cost Price = 25.75 - 25.00 = 0.75\n   - Since the selling price is greater than the cost price, there is a profit.\n\n3. **Calculate the Profit Percentage:**\n   - Profit Percentage = \\(\\left(\\frac{\\text{Profit}}{\\text{Cost Price}}\\right) \\times 100\\)\n   - Substitute the values:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Profit Percentage} = \\left(\\frac{0.75}{25.00}\\right) \\times 100 = 3\\%\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, if the book were sold for Rs. 25.75, there would be a 3% profit.\n\nThe correct answer is: **B) 3% Profit**'
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of ways to arrange the three children (Susan, Tim, and Zen) on three identical chairs in a straight line, with the condition that Susan must be on the left of Tim.\n\nFirst, let's consider all possible arrangements of the three children without any conditions. Since there are 3 children, the total number of permutations is given by the factorial of 3:\n\n\\[ 3! = 3 \\times 2 \\times 1 = 6 \\]\n\nThese arrangements are:\n1. Susan, Tim, Zen\n2. Susan, Zen, Tim\n3. Tim, Susan, Zen\n4. Tim, Zen, Susan\n5. Zen, Susan, Tim\n6. Zen, Tim, Susan\n\nNext, we apply the condition that Susan must be on the left of Tim. We will go through each arrangement and check if it satisfies this condition:\n\n1. Susan, Tim, Zen (Susan is on the left of Tim)\n2. Susan, Zen, Tim (Susan is on the left of Tim)\n3. Tim, Susan, Zen (Susan is not on the left of Tim)\n4. Tim, Zen, Susan (Susan is not on the left of Tim)\n5. Zen, Susan, Tim (Susan is on the left of Tim)\n6. Zen, Tim, Susan (Susan is not on the left of Tim)\n\nFrom the list above, the arrangements that satisfy the condition are:\n- Susan, Tim, Zen\n- Susan, Zen, Tim\n- Zen, Susan, Tim\n\nThus, there are 3 arrangements where Susan is on the left of Tim.\n\nTherefore, the answer is B) 3."
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the fixed and variable components of the telephone bill. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem:**\n   - The telephone bill is composed of a fixed part and a variable part that depends on the number of calls.\n   - For 540 calls, the bill is Rs.1800.\n   - For 620 calls, the bill is Rs.2040.\n   - We need to find the bill for 500 calls.\n\n2. **Setting Up Equations:**\n   - Let \\( F \\) be the fixed part of the bill.\n   - Let \\( V \\) be the variable cost per call.\n   - For 540 calls: \\( F + 540V = 1800 \\)\n   - For 620 calls: \\( F + 620V = 2040 \\)\n\n3. **Solving the Equations:**\n   - Subtract the first equation from the second to eliminate \\( F \\):\n     \\[\n     (F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     80V = 240\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     V = \\frac{240}{80} = 3\n     \\]\n   - Now that we have \\( V = 3 \\), substitute back into one of the original equations to find \\( F \\):\n     \\[\n     F + 540 \\times 3 = 1800\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     F + 1620 = 1800\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     F = 1800 - 1620 = 180\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculating the Bill for 500 Calls:**\n   - Use the values of \\( F \\) and \\( V \\) to find the bill for 500 calls:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Bill} = F + 500V = 180 + 500 \\times 3\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\text{Bill} = 180 + 1500 = 1680\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The bill for a month in which 500 calls are made is Rs.1680.\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is **B) Rs.1680**."
'To solve this problem, we need to determine when both balls A and B will be at the starting point again after starting from the same point. This involves finding the least common multiple (LCM) of the times it takes for each ball to complete one full rotation.\n\n**Step 1: Determine the time for one full rotation for each ball.**\n\n- **Ball A:**  \n  Ball A makes 2 full rotations in 26 minutes.  \n  Therefore, the time for one full rotation for Ball A is:  \n  \\[\n  \\frac{26 \\text{ minutes}}{2} = 13 \\text{ minutes}\n  \\]\n\n- **Ball B:**  \n  Ball B makes 5 full rotations in 35 minutes.  \n  Therefore, the time for one full rotation for Ball B is:  \n  \\[\n  \\frac{35 \\text{ minutes}}{5} = 7 \\text{ minutes}\n  \\]\n\n**Step 2: Find the least common multiple (LCM) of the rotation times.**\n\nWe need to find the LCM of 13 minutes and 7 minutes.\n\n- The prime factorization of 13 is \\(13\\) (since 13 is a prime number).\n- The prime factorization of 7 is \\(7\\) (since 7 is a prime number).\n\nSince 13 and 7 are both prime numbers and have no common factors other than 1, the LCM is simply their product:\n\\[\n\\text{LCM}(13, 7) = 13 \\times 7 = 91 \\text{ minutes}\n\\]\n\n**Step 3: Convert the LCM into hours and minutes.**\n\n91 minutes can be converted into hours and minutes as follows:\n- 1 hour = 60 minutes\n- 91 minutes = 1 hour and 31 minutes (since 91 - 60 = 31)\n\nTherefore, both balls A and B will be at the starting point again after 1 hour and 31 minutes.\n\n**Answer: A) 1 hour and 31 minutes**'
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the maximum number of books that can be both hardcover and fiction. We can use the principle of inclusion-exclusion to help us.\n\nLet's define:\n- \\( H \\) as the set of hardcover books.\n- \\( F \\) as the set of fiction books.\n\nWe are given:\n- Total number of books, \\( |H \\cup F| = 45 \\).\n- Number of hardcover books, \\( |H| = 30 \\).\n- Number of fiction books, \\( |F| = 20 \\).\n\nWe want to find the maximum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction, which is \\( |H \\cap F| \\).\n\nUsing the principle of inclusion-exclusion, we have:\n\\[\n|H \\cup F| = |H| + |F| - |H \\cap F|\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\\[\n45 = 30 + 20 - |H \\cap F|\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n\\[\n45 = 50 - |H \\cap F|\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( |H \\cap F| \\):\n\\[\n|H \\cap F| = 50 - 45 = 5\n\\]\n\nHowever, this calculation gives us the minimum number of books that are both hardcover and fiction, not the maximum. To find the maximum, we need to consider the constraints:\n\n- The maximum number of books that can be both hardcover and fiction is limited by the smaller of the two categories, which is the fiction books, since there are only 20 fiction books.\n\nTherefore, the maximum number of books that can be both hardcover and fiction is 20.\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{20}\\)."
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information provided in the hint:\n\n1. **Cost of Newspapers:**\n   - Sunday: $4 per newspaper\n   - Monday through Saturday: $1 per newspaper\n\n2. **Order Pattern:**\n   - The hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does on any other day of the week.\n\n3. **Total Weekly Cost:**\n   - The hotel spends $210 per week on newspapers.\n\nLet's define the number of newspapers the hotel buys on Monday (and each of the other weekdays) as \\( x \\).\n\n4. **Newspapers Ordered:**\n   - Monday through Saturday: \\( x \\) newspapers each day\n   - Sunday: \\( 2x \\) newspapers\n\n5. **Cost Calculation:**\n   - Cost for Monday through Saturday: \\( 6 \\times x \\times 1 = 6x \\)\n   - Cost for Sunday: \\( 2x \\times 4 = 8x \\)\n\n6. **Total Weekly Cost Equation:**\n   \\[\n   6x + 8x = 210\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   14x = 210\n   \\]\n\n7. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{210}{14} = 15\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the hotel buys 15 newspapers on Monday.\n\nThe correct answer is: **A) 15**"
"To solve this problem, let's follow the steps:\n\n1. **Define Variables:**\n   - Let \\( x \\) be the original number of friends who planned to go on the picnic.\n\n2. **Initial Contribution:**\n   - If all \\( x \\) friends attended, each would contribute \\( \\frac{96}{x} \\) rupees.\n\n3. **Change in Situation:**\n   - Four friends did not attend, so the number of friends who actually attended is \\( x - 4 \\).\n\n4. **New Contribution:**\n   - The remaining friends had to contribute Rs. 4 extra each, so each of them contributed \\( \\frac{96}{x} + 4 \\) rupees.\n\n5. **Equation Setup:**\n   - The total contribution by the remaining friends is still Rs. 96. Therefore, we can set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     (x - 4) \\left(\\frac{96}{x} + 4\\right) = 96\n     \\]\n\n6. **Simplify the Equation:**\n   - Distribute the terms:\n     \\[\n     (x - 4) \\cdot \\frac{96}{x} + 4(x - 4) = 96\n     \\]\n   - Simplify:\n     \\[\n     96 - \\frac{384}{x} + 4x - 16 = 96\n     \\]\n   - Combine like terms:\n     \\[\n     4x - \\frac{384}{x} = 16\n     \\]\n\n7. **Clear the Fraction:**\n   - Multiply through by \\( x \\) to eliminate the fraction:\n     \\[\n     4x^2 - 384 = 16x\n     \\]\n\n8. **Rearrange the Equation:**\n   - Bring all terms to one side:\n     \\[\n     4x^2 - 16x - 384 = 0\n     \\]\n\n9. **Simplify the Quadratic Equation:**\n   - Divide the entire equation by 4:\n     \\[\n     x^2 - 4x - 96 = 0\n     \\]\n\n10. **Solve the Quadratic Equation:**\n    - Use the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = -96 \\):\n    \\[\n    x = \\frac{-(-4) \\pm \\sqrt{(-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-96)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n    \\]\n    \\[\n    x = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 384}}{2}\n    \\]\n    \\[\n    x = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{400}}{2}\n    \\]\n    \\[\n    x = \\frac{4 \\pm 20}{2}\n    \\]\n\n11. **Calculate the Roots:**\n    - \\( x = \\frac{4 + 20}{2} = 12 \\)\n    - \\( x = \\frac{4 - 20}{2} = -8 \\) (not possible since the number of friends cannot be negative)\n\n12. **Conclusion:**\n    - The original number of friends was 12. Since 4 did not attend, the number of friends who attended the picnic is \\( 12 - 4 = 8 \\).\n\nTherefore, the number of friends who attended the picnic is \\( \\boxed{8} \\)."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint:\n\n1. **Original Shape and Dimensions**: The wire is originally in the shape of a rectangle with a length of 27 cm and a breadth of 17 cm.\n\n2. **Calculate the Perimeter of the Rectangle**:  \n   The formula for the perimeter of a rectangle is:  \n   \\[\n   \\text{Perimeter} = 2 \\times (\\text{length} + \\text{breadth})\n   \\]  \n   Substituting the given values:  \n   \\[\n   \\text{Perimeter} = 2 \\times (27 \\, \\text{cm} + 17 \\, \\text{cm}) = 2 \\times 44 \\, \\text{cm} = 88 \\, \\text{cm}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Rebend the Wire to Form a Square**:  \n   The perimeter of the square formed by rebending the wire is equal to the perimeter of the rectangle, which is 88 cm.\n\n4. **Calculate the Side Length of the Square**:  \n   The formula for the perimeter of a square is:  \n   \\[\n   \\text{Perimeter} = 4 \\times \\text{side length}\n   \\]  \n   Setting this equal to the perimeter of the rectangle:  \n   \\[\n   4 \\times \\text{side length} = 88 \\, \\text{cm}\n   \\]  \n   Solving for the side length:  \n   \\[\n   \\text{side length} = \\frac{88 \\, \\text{cm}}{4} = 22 \\, \\text{cm}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the measure of each side of the square is 22 cm. The correct answer is:  \nC) 22"
"To solve this problem, we need to determine how much each daughter receives based on the given conditions. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Define Variables:**\n   - Let the amount each nephew receives be \\( x \\).\n\n2. **Determine Amounts for Daughters and Sons:**\n   - Each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, so each daughter receives \\( 4x \\).\n   - Each son receives five times as much as each nephew, so each son receives \\( 5x \\).\n\n3. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - There are 2 nephews, 4 daughters, and 5 sons.\n   - The total amount distributed is Rs 8600.\n   - The equation based on the distribution is:\n     \\[\n     2x + 4(4x) + 5(5x) = 8600\n     \\]\n\n4. **Simplify the Equation:**\n   - Calculate the total amount for daughters: \\( 4 \\times 4x = 16x \\).\n   - Calculate the total amount for sons: \\( 5 \\times 5x = 25x \\).\n   - Substitute these into the equation:\n     \\[\n     2x + 16x + 25x = 8600\n     \\]\n   - Combine like terms:\n     \\[\n     43x = 8600\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\( x \\):**\n   - Divide both sides by 43 to find \\( x \\):\n     \\[\n     x = \\frac{8600}{43} = 200\n     \\]\n\n6. **Calculate the Amount Each Daughter Receives:**\n   - Each daughter receives \\( 4x \\):\n     \\[\n     4x = 4 \\times 200 = 800\n     \\]\n\nTherefore, each daughter receives Rs 800. The correct answer is:\n\nE) Rs 800"

"To solve this problem, we need to use the properties of an arithmetic progression (A.P.) and the information given in the question. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the A.P. setup:**\n   - The ages of the members are in an arithmetic progression.\n   - The common difference is 3 months, which is equivalent to 0.25 years.\n   - The youngest member is 7 years old.\n\n2. **Define the terms of the A.P.:**\n   - Let the number of members be \\( n \\).\n   - The first term \\( a \\) of the A.P. is 7 years (the age of the youngest member).\n   - The common difference \\( d \\) is 0.25 years.\n\n3. **Write the expression for the sum of the A.P.:**\n   - The sum of the ages of all members is given by the formula for the sum of an A.P.:\n     \\[\n     S_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2a + (n-1)d)\n     \\]\n   - We know \\( S_n = 250 \\), \\( a = 7 \\), and \\( d = 0.25 \\).\n\n4. **Substitute the known values into the sum formula:**\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2 \\times 7 + (n-1) \\times 0.25)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (14 + 0.25n - 0.25)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (13.75 + 0.25n)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   500 = n \\times (13.75 + 0.25n)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   500 = 13.75n + 0.25n^2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Rearrange the equation to form a quadratic equation:**\n   \\[\n   0.25n^2 + 13.75n - 500 = 0\n   \\]\n\n6. **Multiply the entire equation by 4 to eliminate the decimal:**\n   \\[\n   n^2 + 55n - 2000 = 0\n   \\]\n\n7. **Solve the quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:**\n   - The quadratic formula is \\( n = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 55 \\), and \\( c = -2000 \\).\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-55 \\pm \\sqrt{55^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-2000)}}{2 \\times 1}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-55 \\pm \\sqrt{3025 + 8000}}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-55 \\pm \\sqrt{11025}}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-55 \\pm 105}{2}\n   \\]\n\n8. **Calculate the possible values for \\( n \\):**\n   - \\( n = \\frac{-55 + 105}{2} = \\frac{50}{2} = 25 \\)\n   - \\( n = \\frac{-55 - 105}{2} = \\frac{-160}{2} = -80 \\) (not possible since \\( n \\) must be positive)\n\nTherefore, the number of members in the club is \\( \\boxed{25} \\)."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and calculate the additional contribution required per remaining man.\n\n1. **Initial number of men**: \\( M \\)\n2. **Total cost of the gift**: Rs. \\( D \\)\n3. **Number of men who drop out**: 3\n4. **Remaining number of men**: \\( M - 3 \\)\n\n5. **Initial contribution per man**: \n   \\[\n   \\frac{D}{M}\n   \\]\n\n6. **New contribution per man after 3 men drop out**: \n   \\[\n   \\frac{D}{M-3}\n   \\]\n\n7. **Additional contribution required per remaining man**: \n   \\[\n   \\left(\\frac{D}{M-3}\\right) - \\left(\\frac{D}{M}\\right)\n   \\]\n\n   To simplify this expression, find a common denominator:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{D(M) - D(M-3)}{M(M-3)}\n   \\]\n\n   Simplify the numerator:\n   \\[\n   DM - D(M-3) = DM - DM + 3D = 3D\n   \\]\n\n   So, the expression becomes:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{3D}{M(M-3)}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the additional contribution required per remaining man is:\n\\[\n\\frac{3D}{M^2 - 3M}\n\\]\n\nThe correct answer is:\nD) \\(\\frac{3D}{M^2 - 3M}\\)"
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the marked price of the sewing machine such that after offering a 20% discount, Karan still makes a 20% profit on the cost price. Let's break down the steps:\n\n1. **Cost Price (CP) of the sewing machine**: Rs. 1200\n\n2. **Desired Profit Percentage**: 20%\n\n3. **Calculate the Selling Price (SP) for a 20% profit**:\n   - Profit = 20% of Cost Price = 0.20 * Rs. 1200 = Rs. 240\n   - Selling Price (SP) = Cost Price + Profit = Rs. 1200 + Rs. 240 = Rs. 1440\n\n4. **Discount Offered on the Marked Price**: 20%\n\n5. **Relation between Marked Price (MP) and Selling Price (SP)**:\n   - Selling Price after 20% discount = 80% of Marked Price\n   - Therefore, SP = 0.80 * MP\n\n6. **Set up the equation to find the Marked Price (MP)**:\n   - We know SP = Rs. 1440\n   - So, 0.80 * MP = Rs. 1440\n\n7. **Solve for Marked Price (MP)**:\n   - MP = Rs. 1440 / 0.80\n   - MP = Rs. 1800\n\nTherefore, Karan should mark the sewing machine at Rs. 1800 to ensure that after offering a 20% discount, he still makes a 20% profit.\n\nThe correct answer is: **E) 1,800**"

Let's break down the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Departure and Speed Information:**\n   - Train A departs from Mumbai Central at 11 am and travels at a speed of 40 kmph.\n   - Train B departs from Mumbai Central at 2 pm and travels at a speed of 72 kmph.\n\n2. **Time Difference:**\n   - Train A leaves 3 hours earlier than Train B (from 11 am to 2 pm).\n\n3. **Distance Covered by Train A before Train B Starts:**\n   - In 3 hours, Train A will cover a distance of:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Distance} = \\text{Speed} \\times \\text{Time} = 40 \\, \\text{kmph} \\times 3 \\, \\text{hours} = 120 \\, \\text{km}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Relative Speed:**\n   - Since both trains are moving in the same direction, the relative speed between Train B and Train A is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Relative Speed} = 72 \\, \\text{kmph} - 40 \\, \\text{kmph} = 32 \\, \\text{kmph}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Time Taken for Train B to Catch Up:**\n   - Train B needs to cover the 120 km head start that Train A has. The time taken for Train B to catch up is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Time} = \\frac{\\text{Distance}}{\\text{Relative Speed}} = \\frac{120 \\, \\text{km}}{32 \\, \\text{kmph}} = 3.75 \\, \\text{hours}\n     \\]\n\n6. **Meeting Time:**\n   - Train B starts at 2 pm. The correct answer is \\( \\boxed{60} \\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to understand the doubling process of the water lilies and how it affects the time taken to cover the lake.\n\n1. **Understanding the Doubling Process:**\n   - The number of water lilies doubles every two days.\n   - Starting with 1 water lily, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Number of Doublings:**\n   - Since the number of water lilies doubles every two days, the number of doublings in 60 days is \\( \\frac{60}{2} = 30 \\) doublings.\n\n3. **Determine the Total Number of Water Lilies:**\n   - After 30 doublings, starting from 1 water lily, the total number of water lilies is \\( 2^{30} \\).\n\n4. **Starting with 64 Water Lilies:**\n   - 64 is \\( 2^6 \\) (since \\( 2^6 = 64 \\)).\n   - This means starting with 64 water lilies is equivalent to starting with \\( 2^6 \\) water lilies.\n\n5. **Calculate the Remaining Doublings Needed:**\n   - If we start with \\( 2^6 \\) water lilies, we need \\( 30 - 6 = 24 \\) more doublings to reach \\( 2^{30} \\) water lilies.\n\n6. **Calculate the Time for 24 Doublings:**\n   - Since each doubling takes 2 days, 24 doublings will take \\( 24 \\times 2 = 48 \\) days.\n\nTherefore, if we start with 64 water lilies, it will take 48 days for the lake to be fully covered.\n\nThe correct answer is not listed in the provided answer choices, but based on the calculations, the lake will be fully covered in 48 days.'
"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step using the information and hints provided:\n\n1. **Understanding the given scenario:**\n   - \\( x \\) men working \\( x \\) hours per day can complete \\( x \\) units of work in \\( x \\) days.\n   - Using the formula for work done: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Work} = \\text{Number of Men} \\times \\text{Hours per Day} \\times \\text{Number of Days}\n     \\]\n   - For \\( x \\) men working \\( x \\) hours per day for \\( x \\) days, the work done is:\n     \\[\n     x \\times x \\times x = x^3 \\text{ units}\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, \\( x^3 \\) units of work corresponds to \\( x \\) units of work, meaning:\n     \\[\n     x^3 = x\n     \\]\n   - This implies that the work done per unit is \\( x^2 \\).\n\n2. **Finding the work done by \\( y \\) men:**\n   - We need to find how much work \\( y \\) men working \\( y \\) hours per day can complete in \\( y \\) days.\n   - Using the same formula for work done:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Work} = y \\times y \\times y = y^3 \\text{ units}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Relating the work done by \\( y \\) men to the work done by \\( x \\) men:**\n   - We know that \\( x^3 \\) units of work is equivalent to \\( x \\) units of work.\n   - Therefore, the work done by \\( y \\) men in terms of the work done by \\( x \\) men is:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{y^3}{x^2} \\text{ units}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - The amount of work that can be completed by \\( y \\) men working \\( y \\) hours per day in \\( y \\) days is:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{y^3}{x^2} \\text{ units}\n     \\]\n\nThus, the correct answer is \\( \\boxed{\\frac{y^3}{x^2}} \\), which corresponds to option B."
"To solve the problem of determining how many different quadrilaterals can be formed by joining 4 of the points A, B, C, D, E, and F, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify the Points**: We have 6 points available: A, B, C, D, E, and F.\n\n2. **Understand the Requirement**: We need to form quadrilaterals, which require selecting 4 points out of the 6 available.\n\n3. **Use Combinatorial Formula**: The number of ways to choose 4 points from 6 is given by the combination formula \\(\\binom{n}{k}\\), where \\(n\\) is the total number of points, and \\(k\\) is the number of points to choose.\n\n4. **Calculate the Combinations**:\n   \\[\n   \\binom{6}{4} = \\frac{6!}{4!(6-4)!} = \\frac{6 \\times 5}{2 \\times 1} = 15\n   \\]\n\n5. **List the Combinations**: To ensure understanding, let's list the combinations of points that form quadrilaterals:\n   - ABCD\n   - ABCE\n   - ABCF\n   - ABDE\n   - ABDF\n   - ABEF\n   - ACDE\n   - ACDF\n   - ACEF\n   - ADEF\n   - BCDE\n   - BCDF\n   - BCEF\n   - BDEF\n   - CDEF\n\n6. **Verify the Count**: We have listed 15 different combinations, confirming our calculation.\n\nTherefore, the number of different quadrilaterals that can be formed is \\(\\boxed{15}\\)."
"To solve the problem, let's break it down step by step using the given information:\n\n1. **Points on the Circle**: Points A, B, C, D lie in this order on the circumference of a circle.\n\n2. **Arc AC**: The measure of minor arc AC is 160°.\n\n3. **Arc BD**: The measure of minor arc BD is 150°.\n\n4. **B Bisects Arc AC**: Point B bisects minor arc AC, meaning arc AB = arc BC.\n\n5. **Find Arc AD**: We need to find the measure of minor arc AD.\n\n**Step-by-Step Solution**:\n\n- Since B bisects minor arc AC, arc AB = arc BC. Therefore, each of these arcs is half of arc AC:\n  \\[\n  \\text{Arc AB} = \\text{Arc BC} = \\frac{160°}{2} = 80°\n  \\]\n\n- Now, we know:\n  - Arc AB = 80°\n  - Arc BC = 80°\n  - Arc BD = 150°\n\n- Since points A, B, C, D are in this order on the circle, arc AD is composed of arc AB and arc BD:\n  \\[\n  \\text{Arc AD} = \\text{Arc AB} + \\text{Arc BD} = 80° + 150° = 230°\n  \\]\n\n- However, 230° is not a minor arc. Since the total circle is 360°, the minor arc AD is the smaller arc between A and D, which is:\n  \\[\n  \\text{Minor Arc AD} = 360° - 230° = 130°\n  \\]\n\nThus, the measure of minor arc AD is 130°.\n\n**Answer**: B) 130°"

'To find the depth of the canal, we can use the formula for the area of a trapezium (trapezoid):\n\n\\[\n\\text{Area} = \\frac{1}{2} \\times (\\text{Base}_1 + \\text{Base}_2) \\times \\text{Height}\n\\]\n\nWhere:\n- \\(\\text{Base}_1\\) is the width at the top of the trapezium.\n- \\(\\text{Base}_2\\) is the width at the bottom of the trapezium.\n- \\(\\text{Height}\\) is the depth of the canal, which we need to find.\n\nGiven:\n- \\(\\text{Base}_1 = 10\\) meters\n- \\(\\text{Base}_2 = 6\\) meters\n- \\(\\text{Area} = 640\\) square meters\n\nSubstitute these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n640 = \\frac{1}{2} \\times (10 + 6) \\times \\text{Height}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\n640 = \\frac{1}{2} \\times 16 \\times \\text{Height}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n640 = 8 \\times \\text{Height}\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\(\\text{Height}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{Height} = \\frac{640}{8} = 80\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the depth of the canal is 80 meters.\n\nThe correct answer is D) 80.'

"To solve this problem, we need to calculate the distance traveled by a point on the edge of a fan blade. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Identify the radius of the circle:**\n   - The point is 10 centimeters from the center of the fan, so the radius \\( r \\) is 10 cm.\n\n2. **Calculate the circumference of the circle:**\n   - The circumference \\( C \\) of a circle is given by the formula \\( C = 2\\pi r \\).\n   - Substituting the radius, \\( C = 2\\pi \\times 10 = 20\\pi \\) cm.\n\n3. **Determine the number of revolutions in 30 seconds:**\n   - The fan rotates at a rate of 300 revolutions per minute.\n   - Since there are 60 seconds in a minute, the fan makes \\( \\frac{300}{60} = 5 \\) revolutions per second.\n   - In 30 seconds, the number of revolutions is \\( 5 \\times 30 = 150 \\).\n\n4. **Calculate the total distance traveled:**\n   - The distance traveled in one revolution is the circumference of the circle, which is \\( 20\\pi \\) cm.\n   - Therefore, the total distance traveled in 150 revolutions is \\( 150 \\times 20\\pi = 3000\\pi \\) cm.\n\nThus, the distance traveled by the point on the edge of the fan blade after 30 seconds is \\( \\boxed{3000\\pi} \\) cm."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine how many months after B joined the business, C joined. Let's break down the information and solve it step by step.\n\n1. **Initial Investments and Timelines:**\n   - A starts the business with Rs.40,000.\n   - B joins 2 months later with Rs.60,000.\n   - C joins with Rs.120,000 at some point after B.\n\n2. **Profit Sharing:**\n   - Total profit at the end of the year is Rs.375,000.\n   - C's share of the profit is Rs.150,000.\n\n3. **Understanding Profit Sharing:**\n   - The profit is shared based on the amount of capital invested and the time for which it is invested.\n   - Let's denote the number of months C was in the business as \\( x \\).\n\n4. **Calculate the Time-Weighted Investments:**\n   - A's investment is for 12 months: \\( 40,000 \\times 12 = 480,000 \\)\n   - B's investment is for \\( 12 - 2 = 10 \\) months: \\( 60,000 \\times 10 = 600,000 \\)\n   - C's investment is for \\( x \\) months: \\( 120,000 \\times x = 120,000x \\)\n\n5. **Total Profit Sharing Ratio:**\n   - The ratio of their investments is \\( 480,000 : 600,000 : 120,000x \\).\n\n6. **C's Share of the Profit:**\n   - C's share of the profit is given as Rs.150,000 out of Rs.375,000.\n   - Therefore, C's share in the ratio is \\( \\frac{150,000}{375,000} = \\frac{2}{5} \\).\n\n7. **Setting Up the Equation:**\n   - The ratio of C's investment to the total investment should be \\( \\frac{2}{5} \\).\n   - Total investment = \\( 480,000 + 600,000 + 120,000x \\).\n   - C's investment share: \\( \\frac{120,000x}{480,000 + 600,000 + 120,000x} = \\frac{2}{5} \\).\n\n8. **Solving the Equation:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{120,000x}{1,080,000 + 120,000x} = \\frac{2}{5}\n   \\]\n   Cross-multiply to solve for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   5 \\times 120,000x = 2 \\times (1,080,000 + 120,000x)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   600,000x = 2,160,000 + 240,000x\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   600,000x - 240,000x = 2,160,000\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   360,000x = 2,160,000\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{2,160,000}{360,000} = 6\n   \\]\n\n9. **Conclusion:**\n   - C joined the business 6 months after B joined.\n\nTherefore, the answer is **B) 4 months** after B joined the business, C joined."

"To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Journey:**\n   - Kevin drives from A to B at 70 mph.\n   - He returns from B to A at 90 mph.\n   - 3 hours before the end of his trip, he is 70 miles away from B.\n\n2. **Calculate the Time to Reach B:**\n   - Let \\( d \\) be the distance between A and B.\n   - The time taken to travel from A to B is \\( \\frac{d}{70} \\) hours.\n\n3. **Calculate the Time to Return to A:**\n   - The time taken to travel from B to A is \\( \\frac{d}{90} \\) hours.\n\n4. **Total Time for the Trip:**\n   - The total time for the round trip is \\( \\frac{d}{70} + \\frac{d}{90} \\).\n\n5. **Condition Given in the Problem:**\n   - 3 hours before the end of the trip, Kevin is 70 miles away from B.\n   - At 70 mph, it takes him \\( \\frac{70}{70} = 1 \\) hour to reach B from that point.\n\n6. **Calculate the Remaining Time:**\n   - After reaching B, he still has to return to A.\n   - The time to return from B to A is \\( \\frac{d}{90} \\).\n\n7. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - The total time for the trip minus the 3 hours (when he was 70 miles away from B) is equal to the time taken to reach B from that point (1 hour) plus the time to return to A.\n   - Therefore, \\( \\frac{d}{70} + \\frac{d}{90} - 3 = 1 + \\frac{d}{90} \\).\n\n8. **Simplify the Equation:**\n   - \\( \\frac{d}{70} - 3 = 1 \\).\n   - \\( \\frac{d}{70} = 4 \\).\n   - \\( d = 4 \\times 70 = 280 \\).\n\n9. **Verify the Solution:**\n   - The distance from A to B is 280 miles.\n   - Time from A to B: \\( \\frac{280}{70} = 4 \\) hours.\n   - Time from B to A: \\( \\frac{280}{90} \\approx 3.11 \\) hours.\n   - Total time: \\( 4 + 3.11 = 7.11 \\) hours.\n   - 3 hours before the end of the trip, Kevin is 70 miles away from B, which checks out with the given condition.\n\nTherefore, the distance between A and B is 280 miles. Since this is not one of the answer choices, the correct answer is:\n\nE) None of the above"

'To solve the problem, we need to determine the amount of zinc and copper in alloys X and Y, and then combine them to find the ratio in alloy Z.\n\n### Step 1: Determine the composition of Alloy X\n- Alloy X has a zinc to copper ratio of 6:9.\n- Total parts = 6 + 9 = 15 parts.\n\nFor 40 grams of alloy X:\n- Zinc in X = \\(\\frac{6}{15} \\times 40 = 16\\) grams\n- Copper in X = \\(\\frac{9}{15} \\times 40 = 24\\) grams\n\n### Step 2: Determine the composition of Alloy Y\n- Alloy Y has a zinc to copper ratio of 7:11.\n- Total parts = 7 + 11 = 18 parts.\n\nFor 60 grams of alloy Y:\n- Zinc in Y = \\(\\frac{7}{18} \\times 60 = 23.33\\) grams\n- Copper in Y = \\(\\frac{11}{18} \\times 60 = 36.67\\) grams\n\n### Step 3: Combine the alloys to form Alloy Z\n- Total zinc in Z = Zinc in X + Zinc in Y = 16 + 23.33 = 39.33 grams\n- Total copper in Z = Copper in X + Copper in Y = 24 + 36.67 = 60.67 grams\n\n### Step 4: Calculate the ratio of zinc to copper in Alloy Z\n- Ratio of zinc to copper in Z = 39.33 : 60.67\n\nTo simplify the ratio, we can multiply both parts by 3 to avoid decimals:\n- Zinc = 39.33 × 3 = 118\n- Copper = 60.67 × 3 = 182\n\nThus, the simplified ratio of zinc to copper in alloy Z is approximately 59:91.\n\nTherefore, the answer is:\n**D) 59:91**'
"To determine how many senators can be considered Hoopsmot's based on his contribution, we can follow these steps:\n\n1. **Identify Total Contributions:**\n   - Hoopsmot contributes $16,000.\n   - Smolapon contributes $4,000.\n   - Total contribution = $16,000 + $4,000 = $20,000.\n\n2. **Determine the Total Number of Senators Influenced:**\n   - The total contribution of $20,000 allows them to influence 30 senators.\n\n3. **Calculate the Cost per Senator:**\n   - Cost per senator = Total contribution / Total number of senators influenced\n   - Cost per senator = $20,000 / 30 = $666.67 per senator.\n\n4. **Calculate the Number of Senators Hoopsmot Can Influence:**\n   - Hoopsmot's contribution = $16,000.\n   - Number of senators Hoopsmot can influence = Hoopsmot's contribution / Cost per senator\n   - Number of senators Hoopsmot can influence = $16,000 / $666.67 ≈ 24.\n\nTherefore, the number of senators that can be considered Hoopsmot's based on his contribution is 24.\n\nThe correct answer is: **D) 24**."
"To solve the problem, we need to find two numbers, let's call them \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), such that:\n\n1. The difference between their squares is 256,000: \n   \\[\n   x^2 - y^2 = 256,000\n   \\]\n\n2. The sum of the numbers is 1,000:\n   \\[\n   x + y = 1,000\n   \\]\n\nWe can use the identity for the difference of squares:\n\\[\nx^2 - y^2 = (x + y)(x - y)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given sum of the numbers into the identity:\n\\[\n(x + y)(x - y) = 256,000\n\\]\n\\[\n1,000(x - y) = 256,000\n\\]\n\nNow, solve for \\( x - y \\):\n\\[\nx - y = \\frac{256,000}{1,000} = 256\n\\]\n\nNow we have a system of two equations:\n1. \\( x + y = 1,000 \\)\n2. \\( x - y = 256 \\)\n\nWe can solve this system by adding the two equations:\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 1,000 + 256\n\\]\n\\[\n2x = 1,256\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{1,256}{2} = 628\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 628 \\) back into the equation \\( x + y = 1,000 \\):\n\\[\n628 + y = 1,000\n\\]\n\\[\ny = 1,000 - 628 = 372\n\\]\n\nThus, the two numbers are 628 and 372. "To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the total income, median income, and the number of family members.\n\n1. **Understanding the Median**: \n   - The median income is the middle value when all incomes are arranged in order. \n   - If the number of family members is odd, the median is the income of the middle member.\n   - If the number of family members is even, the median is the average of the two middle incomes.\n\n2. **Given Information**:\n   - Total income of the family per month = $9000\n   - Median income = $3000\n\n3. **Determine the Number of Family Members**:\n   - Let's denote the number of family members as \\( n \\).\n   - If the median income is $3000, then the middle income (or the average of the two middle incomes) is $3000.\n\n4. **Analyzing the Options**:\n   - **Option A: 2 members**  \n     - If there are 2 members, the median would be the average of the two incomes. For the median to be $3000, both incomes would need to be $3000. However, this would only total $6000, not $9000.\n   \n   - **Option B: 3 members**  \n     - If there are 3 members, the median is the income of the second member when arranged in order. For the median to be $3000, the second member's income must be $3000. The total income could be distributed as $3000, $3000, $3000, which totals $9000. This works.\n   \n   - **Option C: 4 members**  \n     - If there are 4 members, the median is the average of the second and third incomes. For the median to be $3000, the average of the second and third incomes must be $3000. This could be $3000, $3000, $3000, $3000, which totals $12000, not $9000.\n   \n   - **Option D: 5 members**  \n     - If there are 5 members, the median is the income of the third member. For the median to be $3000, the third member's income must be $3000. The total income could be distributed as $3000, $3000, $3000, $0, $3000, which totals $9000. This works.\n   \n   - **Option E: 6 members**  \n     - If there are 6 members, the median is the average of the third and fourth incomes. For the median to be $3000, the average of the third and fourth incomes must be $3000. This could be $3000, $3000, $3000, $3000, $0, $0, which totals $9000. This works.\n\n5. **Conclusion**:\n   - The number of family members can be 3, 5, or 6 based on the given conditions. However, since the problem asks for a single answer, the most straightforward and simplest distribution is with 3 members.\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\( \\boxed{3} \\)."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum number of copper coins the diver brought up, given that she earned a total of $3.40 from collecting copper and brass coins. Let's break down the problem step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Earnings:**\n   - Each copper coin earns the diver 20 cents.\n   - Each brass coin earns the diver 25 cents.\n   - The total earnings from one dive are $3.40, which is equivalent to 340 cents.\n\n2. **Set Up the Equation:**\n   - Let \\( c \\) be the number of copper coins.\n   - Let \\( b \\) be the number of brass coins.\n   - The equation for the total earnings is:\n     \\[\n     20c + 25b = 340\n     \\]\n\n3. **Solve for the Minimum Number of Copper Coins:**\n   - We need to find the minimum value of \\( c \\) such that the equation holds true with non-negative integer values for both \\( c \\) and \\( b \\).\n\n4. **Trial and Error with Integer Solutions:**\n   - Start with \\( c = 0 \\):\n     \\[\n     20(0) + 25b = 340 \\implies 25b = 340 \\implies b = \\frac{340}{25} = 13.6\n     \\]\n     Since \\( b \\) must be an integer, \\( c = 0 \\) is not possible.\n\n   - Try \\( c = 1 \\):\n     \\[\n     20(1) + 25b = 340 \\implies 20 + 25b = 340 \\implies 25b = 320 \\implies b = \\frac{320}{25} = 12.8\n     \\]\n     Again, \\( b \\) is not an integer, so \\( c = 1 \\) is not possible.\n\n   - Try \\( c = 2 \\):\n     \\[\n     20(2) + 25b = 340 \\implies 40 + 25b = 340 \\implies 25b = 300 \\implies b = \\frac{300}{25} = 12\n     \\]\n     Here, \\( b = 12 \\) is an integer, so \\( c = 2 \\) is a valid solution.\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The minimum number of copper coins the diver brought is \\( c = 2 \\).\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\( \\boxed{2} \\)."

"To find the difference in speed between car 'X' and car 'Y', we need to calculate the speed of each car and then find the difference between these speeds.\n\n**Step 1: Calculate the speed of car 'X'.**\n\nCar 'X' covers a distance of 320 kilometers in 8 hours.  \nSpeed of car 'X' = Distance / Time = 320 km / 8 hours = 40 km/h.\n\n**Step 2: Calculate the speed of car 'Y'.**\n\nCar 'Y' covers a distance of 415 kilometers in 5 hours.  \nSpeed of car 'Y' = Distance / Time = 415 km / 5 hours = 83 km/h.\n\n**Step 3: Calculate the difference in speed between car 'X' and car 'Y'.**\n\nDifference in speed = Speed of car 'Y' - Speed of car 'X' = 83 km/h - 40 km/h = 43 km/h.\n\nTherefore, the difference in the speed of the two cars is 43 km/h.\n\nThe correct answer is: **C) 43 kms/hr**."

Height of the flagstaff = 17.5 meters\n2. Length of the flagstaff's shadow = 40.25 meters\n3. Length of the building's shadow = 28.75 meters\n\nWe need to find the height of the building. "To solve this problem, we need to determine how much time will pass before the two cars are 15 miles apart. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem:**\n   - Car 1 travels at 55 mph.\n   - Car 2 travels at 52 mph.\n   - Both cars start from the same point at the same time.\n   - We need to find the time it takes for the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles.\n\n2. **Determine the Relative Speed:**\n   - Since both cars are traveling in the same direction, the relative speed between the two cars is the difference in their speeds.\n   - Relative speed = Speed of Car 1 - Speed of Car 2 = 55 mph - 52 mph = 3 mph.\n\n3. **Calculate the Time to be 15 Miles Apart:**\n   - We want the distance between the two cars to be 15 miles.\n   - Using the formula: Distance = Speed × Time, we can rearrange it to find Time = Distance / Speed.\n   - Time = 15 miles / 3 mph = 5 hours.\n\nTherefore, the time it will take for the two cars to be 15 miles apart is 5 hours.\n\nThe correct answer is: **B) 5 hours**."
"To solve this problem, we need to use the information given and the properties of probability, especially for independent events. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the Given Information:**\n   - The probability that event A occurs, \\( P(A) \\), is 0.6.\n   - The probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs, \\( P(A \\cup B) \\), is 0.96.\n   - Events A and B are independent.\n\n2. **Use the Formula for the Union of Two Independent Events:**\n   - For two independent events A and B, the probability of their union is given by:\n     \\[\n     P(A \\cup B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A)P(B)\n     \\]\n\n3. **Substitute the Known Values:**\n   - We know \\( P(A \\cup B) = 0.96 \\) and \\( P(A) = 0.6 \\). We need to find \\( P(B) \\).\n   - Substitute these values into the formula:\n     \\[\n     0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 \\times P(B))\n     \\]\n\n4. **Solve for \\( P(B) \\):**\n   - Simplify the equation:\n     \\[\n     0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B)\n     \\]\n   - Combine like terms:\n     \\[\n     0.96 = 0.6 + P(B)(1 - 0.6)\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)\n     \\]\n   - Subtract 0.6 from both sides:\n     \\[\n     0.36 = 0.4P(B)\n     \\]\n   - Divide both sides by 0.4 to solve for \\( P(B) \\):\n     \\[\n     P(B) = \\frac{0.36}{0.4} = 0.9\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The probability that event B occurs, \\( P(B) \\), is 0.9.\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is **E) 0.9**."
"To solve the problem, let's follow the steps outlined in the hint and calculate the ratio of the volume of a cube to the volume of a sphere that fits inside the cube.\n\n1. **Volume of the Cube:**\n   - The side length of the cube is \\( s \\).\n   - The volume of the cube is given by:\n     \\[\n     V_{\\text{cube}} = s^3\n     \\]\n\n2. **Sphere Inside the Cube:**\n   - The sphere that fits inside the cube will have a diameter equal to the side length of the cube, \\( s \\).\n   - Therefore, the radius of the sphere is:\n     \\[\n     r = \\frac{s}{2}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Volume of the Sphere:**\n   - The volume of a sphere with radius \\( r \\) is given by:\n     \\[\n     V_{\\text{sphere}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi r^3\n     \\]\n   - Substituting \\( r = \\frac{s}{2} \\) into the volume formula for the sphere, we get:\n     \\[\n     V_{\\text{sphere}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi \\left(\\frac{s}{2}\\right)^3 = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi \\frac{s^3}{8} = \\frac{\\pi s^3}{6}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Ratio of the Volumes:**\n   - The ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere is:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{V_{\\text{cube}}}{V_{\\text{sphere}}} = \\frac{s^3}{\\frac{\\pi s^3}{6}} = \\frac{6}{\\pi}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere is \\( 6: \\pi \\).\n\nTherefore, the correct answer choice is D) 6: π."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine when the two trains, M and N, cross each other. Let's break down the information and solve it step by step.\n\n1. **Train M's Journey:**\n   - Leaves City A at 5:00 am.\n   - Reaches City B at 9:00 am.\n   - Total travel time = 4 hours.\n\n2. **Train N's Journey:**\n   - Leaves City B at 7:00 am.\n   - Reaches City A at 10:30 am.\n   - Total travel time = 3.5 hours.\n\n3. **Determine the Speeds:**\n   - Assume the distance between City A and City B is \\( D \\).\n   - Speed of Train M = \\( \\frac{D}{4} \\) (since it takes 4 hours to cover distance \\( D \\)).\n   - Speed of Train N = \\( \\frac{D}{3.5} \\) (since it takes 3.5 hours to cover distance \\( D \\)).\n\n4. **Relative Motion:**\n   - Train M starts at 5:00 am, and Train N starts at 7:00 am.\n   - By 7:00 am, Train M has already been traveling for 2 hours.\n   - Distance covered by Train M in 2 hours = \\( 2 \\times \\frac{D}{4} = \\frac{D}{2} \\).\n\n5. **Time Calculation:**\n   - At 7:00 am, Train M is halfway to City B, and Train N starts from City B.\n   - The two trains are now \\( \\frac{D}{2} \\) apart and moving towards each other.\n   - Combined speed of the two trains = Speed of Train M + Speed of Train N = \\( \\frac{D}{4} + \\frac{D}{3.5} \\).\n\n6. **Calculate the Time to Meet:**\n   - Time taken to meet = \\( \\frac{\\text{Distance between them}}{\\text{Combined speed}} \\).\n   - Distance between them = \\( \\frac{D}{2} \\).\n   - Combined speed = \\( \\frac{D}{4} + \\frac{D}{3.5} = \\frac{7D}{28} + \\frac{4D}{14} = \\frac{7D + 8D}{28} = \\frac{15D}{28} \\).\n   - Time taken to meet = \\( \\frac{\\frac{D}{2}}{\\frac{15D}{28}} = \\frac{D}{2} \\times \\frac{28}{15D} = \\frac{28}{30} = \\frac{14}{15} \\) hours.\n\n7. **Convert Time to Minutes:**\n   - \\( \\frac{14}{15} \\) hours = \\( \\frac{14}{15} \\times 60 \\) minutes = 56 minutes.\n\nTherefore, the two trains cross each other 56 minutes after 7:00 am, which is at 7:56 am.\n\nThe correct answer is: **D) 56 min**."

"To solve this problem, we can use the concept of similar triangles. The height of the ant and the length of its shadow form a right triangle, and since both ants are standing side-by-side, the angles of the sun's rays are the same for both ants. Therefore, the triangles are similar, and we can set up a proportion to find the length of the shadow of the taller ant.\n\nLet's list the given information:\n\n1. The first ant is 4 inches tall.\n2. The shadow of the first ant is 10 inches long.\n3. The second ant is 6 inches tall.\n4. We need to find the length of the shadow cast by the 6-inch tall ant.\n\nNow, let's set up the proportion based on the similar triangles:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\text{Height of first ant}}{\\text{Shadow of first ant}} = \\frac{\\text{Height of second ant}}{\\text{Shadow of second ant}}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the known values into the proportion:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{4}{10} = \\frac{6}{x}\n\\]\n\nWhere \\( x \\) is the length of the shadow of the second ant. Now, solve for \\( x \\):\n\n1. Cross-multiply to solve for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   4x = 60\n   \\]\n\n2. The sequence of \\( k \\) consecutive integers starting from \\(-50\\) is: \\(-50, -49, -48, \\ldots, (-50 + k - 1)\\).\n\n2. **Express the sum of these integers:**\n   - The sum of these integers can be expressed as:\n     \\[\n     S = (-50) + (-49) + (-48) + \\ldots + (-50 + k - 1)\n     \\]\n\n3. **Use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic sequence:**\n   - The sum of an arithmetic sequence can be calculated using the formula:\n     \\[\n     S = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (\\text{first term} + \\text{last term})\n     \\]\n   - Here, the first term is \\(-50\\) and the last term is \\(-50 + k - 1\\).\n\n4. **Set up the equation:**\n   - Substitute the known values into the formula:\n     \\[\n     51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times \\left(-50 + (-50 + k - 1)\\right)\n     \\]\n   - Simplify the expression inside the parentheses:\n     \\[\n     51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (-50 - 50 + k - 1)\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (k - 101)\n     \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\( k \\):**\n   - Multiply both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction:\n     \\[\n     102 = k \\times (k - 101)\n     \\]\n   - Expand the equation:\n     \\[\n     102 = k^2 - 101k\n     \\]\n   - Rearrange the equation to form a quadratic equation:\n     \\[\n     k^2 - 101k - 102 = 0\n     \\]\n\n6. **Solve the quadratic equation:**\n   - Use the quadratic formula \\( k = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -101 \\), and \\( c = -102 \\):\n     \\[\n     k = \\frac{-(-101) \\pm \\sqrt{(-101)^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-102)}}{2 \\times 1}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     k = \\frac{101 \\pm \\sqrt{10201 + 408}}{2}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     k = \\frac{101 \\pm \\sqrt{10609}}{2}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     k = \\frac{101 \\pm 103}{2}\n     \\]\n\n   - Calculate the two possible values for \\( k \\):\n     - \\( k = \\frac{101 + 103}{2} = \\frac{204}{2} = 102 \\)\n     - \\( k = \\frac{101 - 103}{2} = \\frac{-2}{2} = -1 \\)\n\n   - Since \\( k \\) must be a positive integer, we choose \\( k = 102 \\).\n\n7. **Conclusion:**\n   - The value of \\( k \\) is 102.\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is \\( \\boxed{102} \\)."

"To solve the problem, we will use Vieta's formulas, which relate the coefficients of a polynomial to sums and products of its roots. Let's go through the steps:\n\n1. **Identify the given information:**\n   - The quadratic equation is \\( x^2 + mx + 22 = 0 \\).\n   - One of the roots is 1.5.\n\n2. **Apply Vieta's formulas:**\n   - For a quadratic equation \\( ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \\), the sum of the roots is given by \\(-b/a\\) and the product of the roots is \\(c/a\\).\n   - In our equation, \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = m \\), and \\( c = 22 \\).\n\n3. **Use the product of the roots:**\n   - Let the roots be \\( r_1 = 1.5 \\) and \\( r_2 \\).\n   - According to Vieta's formulas, the product of the roots is:\n     \\[\n     r_1 \\times r_2 = 22\n     \\]\n   - Substituting the known root:\n     \\[\n     1.5 \\times r_2 = 22\n     \\]\n   - Solve for \\( r_2 \\):\n     \\[\n     r_2 = \\frac{22}{1.5} = \\frac{220}{15} = \\frac{44}{3}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Use the sum of the roots:**\n   - According to Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots is:\n     \\[\n     r_1 + r_2 = -m\n     \\]\n   - Substitute the known values:\n     \\[\n     1.5 + \\frac{44}{3} = -m\n     \\]\n   - Convert 1.5 to a fraction:\n     \\[\n     1.5 = \\frac{3}{2}\n     \\]\n   - Find a common denominator and add the fractions:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{3}{2} + \\frac{44}{3} = \\frac{9}{6} + \\frac{88}{6} = \\frac{97}{6}\n     \\]\n   - Therefore:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{97}{6} = -m\n     \\]\n   - Solve for \\( m \\):\n     \\[\n     m = -\\frac{97}{6} \\approx -16.1667\n     \\]\n\n5. **Choose the closest answer:**\n   - The closest value to \\(-16.1667\\) among the answer choices is \\( -16.2 \\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( m \\) is \\( \\boxed{-16.2} \\)."

"To solve the problem of finding the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made from 28 white and 98 red tulips, we need to determine the greatest common divisor (GCD) of the two numbers, 28 and 98. This will ensure that all flowers are used without any leftovers, and each bouquet will have the same number of white and red tulips.\n\nLet's find the GCD of 28 and 98:\n\n1. **Prime Factorization:**\n   - 28 can be factored into prime numbers as follows:\n     \\[\n     28 = 2^2 \\times 7\n     \\]\n   - 98 can be factored into prime numbers as follows:\n     \\[\n     98 = 2 \\times 7^2\n     \\]\n\n2. **Identify Common Factors:**\n   - The common prime factors of 28 and 98 are 2 and 7.\n\n3. **Determine the GCD:**\n   - For the common prime factor 2, the lowest power is \\(2^1\\).\n   - For the common prime factor 7, the lowest power is \\(7^1\\).\n   - Therefore, the GCD is:\n     \\[\n     GCD = 2^1 \\times 7^1 = 2 \\times 7 = 14\n     \\]\n\nThus, the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made is 14. Each bouquet will have:\n- \\(\\frac{28}{14} = 2\\) white tulips\n- \\(\\frac{98}{14} = 7\\) red tulips\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{14}\\)."

Therefore, \\( |y^2| = y^2 \\).\n- The condition \\( |x^3| > |y^2| \\) translates to \\( -x^3 > y^2 \\).\n\n### Evaluating Each Answer Choice:\n\n**A) \\( x > y \\)**\n\n- Since \\( x < 0 \\) and \\( y > 0 \\), \\( x \\) is negative and \\( y \\) is positive. This statement is not necessarily true.\n\n**C) \\(-x^3 < y^2 \\)**\n\n- We have already established that \\(-x^3 > y^2\\) from the condition \\( |x^3| > |y^2| \\). Therefore, \\( x < -y \\) is true because \\( x \\) is negative and less than any negative number greater in magnitude than \\( x \\). This statement is true.\n\n### Conclusion:\nThe statement that must be true given the conditions is:\n\n**E) \\( x < -y \\)**"

"To solve this problem, we need to maximize the number of trousers purchased with a budget of Rs 810, while also considering the cost of shirts. Let's break down the steps:\n\n1. **Identify the costs:**\n   - Cost of one trouser = Rs 70\n   - Cost of one shirt = Rs 30\n\n2. **Determine the maximum number of trousers that can be purchased:**\n   - If we spend all Rs 810 on trousers, the maximum number of trousers we can buy is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Maximum trousers} = \\left\\lfloor \\frac{810}{70} \\right\\rfloor = 11 \\text{ trousers}\n     \\]\n   - However, buying 11 trousers would cost:\n     \\[\n     11 \\times 70 = 770 \\text{ Rs}\n     \\]\n   - This leaves:\n     \\[\n     810 - 770 = 40 \\text{ Rs}\n     \\]\n   - With Rs 40, we can buy:\n     \\[\n     \\left\\lfloor \\frac{40}{30} \\right\\rfloor = 1 \\text{ shirt}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the ratio of trousers to shirts:**\n   - Number of trousers = 11\n   - Number of shirts = 1\n   - Ratio of trousers to shirts = \\( \\frac{11}{1} = 11:1 \\)\n\n4. **Verify if buying fewer trousers allows for more shirts:**\n   - If we buy 10 trousers, the cost is:\n     \\[\n     10 \\times 70 = 700 \\text{ Rs}\n     \\]\n   - This leaves:\n     \\[\n     810 - 700 = 110 \\text{ Rs}\n     \\]\n   - With Rs 110, we can buy:\n     \\[\n     \\left\\lfloor \\frac{110}{30} \\right\\rfloor = 3 \\text{ shirts}\n     \\]\n   - Ratio of trousers to shirts = \\( \\frac{10}{3} \\approx 3.33:1 \\)\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n   - The maximum number of trousers that can be purchased is 11, with 1 shirt.\n   - The ratio of trousers to shirts when maximizing trousers is 11:1.\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is **E) 11 Trousers**."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine how many times the coin landed on heads such that neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any money after 20 flips.\n\nLet's define:\n- \\( H \\) as the number of times the coin lands on heads.\n- \\( T \\) as the number of times the coin lands on tails.\n\nFrom the problem, we know:\n1. The total number of flips is 20, so:\n   \\[\n   H + T = 20\n   \\]\n\n2. Each time the coin lands on heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan. Therefore, the total amount Christopher gives to Jonathan is \\( 2H \\).\n\n3. Each time the coin lands on tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher. Therefore, the total amount Jonathan gives to Christopher is \\( 3T \\).\n\n4. After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any money, which means the total amount given by Christopher equals the total amount given by Jonathan:\n   \\[\n   2H = 3T\n   \\]\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n1. \\( H + T = 20 \\)\n2. \\( 2H = 3T \\)\n\nWe can solve these equations step by step:\n\nFrom the second equation, express \\( T \\) in terms of \\( H \\):\n\\[\nT = \\frac{2H}{3}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( T = \\frac{2H}{3} \\) into the first equation:\n\\[\nH + \\frac{2H}{3} = 20\n\\]\n\nMultiply the entire equation by 3 to eliminate the fraction:\n\\[\n3H + 2H = 60\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\\[\n5H = 60\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( H \\):\n\\[\nH = \\frac{60}{5} = 12\n\\]\n\nThus, the coin landed on heads 12 times. Therefore, the answer is:\n\nE) 12"

Let's correct it:\n\n- Total distance covered by both in 2 hours should be \\( 2 \\times 132 = 264 \\) km, which is indeed \\( 3D \\).\n- Therefore, the correct calculation should be:\n  \\[\n  3D = 264 \\\\\n  D = \\frac{264}{3} = 88 \\text{ km}\n  \\]\n\nThe correct answer should be 84 km, which matches the closest option D) 84 km."
'To solve this problem, we need to calculate the average cost per year for both new tires and repaired tires, and then determine the percentage by which the average cost per year of new tires is greater than that of repaired tires.\n\n**Step 1: Calculate the average cost per year for new tires.**\n\n- Cost of new tires: $180 per tire\n- Lifespan of new tires: 4 years\n\nAverage cost per year for new tires = Total cost / Lifespan  \n= $180 / 4 years  \n= $45 per year\n\n**Step 2: Calculate the average cost per year for repaired tires.**\n\n- Cost of repairing current tires: $40 per tire\n- Lifespan extension from repair: 1 additional year\n\nAverage cost per year for repaired tires = Total cost / Lifespan extension  \n= $40 / 1 year  \n= $40 per year\n\n**Step 3: Determine the percent by which the average cost per year of new tires is greater than that of repaired tires.**\n\nTo find the percentage increase, use the formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left( \\frac{\\text{New Cost per Year} - \\text{Repaired Cost per Year}}{\\text{Repaired Cost per Year}} \\right) \\times 100\\%\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the values:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left( \\frac{45 - 40}{40} \\right) \\times 100\\%\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\left( \\frac{5}{40} \\right) \\times 100\\%\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 0.125 \\times 100\\%\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 12.5\\%\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the average cost per year of the new tires is 12.5% greater than the cost of repairing the current tires.\n\nThe correct answer is C) 12.5%.'

"To solve this problem, we need to calculate the interest accrued on a bond with semi-annual compounding. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Principal Amount (P):** $5,000\n\n2. **Annual Interest Rate (r):** 12%\n\n3. **Compounding Frequency:** Every six months (semi-annually)\n\n4. **Duration of the Bond:** 1 year\n\n5. **Number of Compounding Periods per Year (n):** Since the interest is compounded semi-annually, there are 2 compounding periods per year.\n\n6. **Total Number of Compounding Periods (t):** Since the bond is for 1 year, and it compounds semi-annually, there are 2 periods in total.\n\n7. **Interest Rate per Period:** The annual interest rate is 12%, so the interest rate per period is 12% / 2 = 6% = 0.06 (as a decimal).\n\nNow, we use the compound interest formula to find the amount at maturity:\n\n\\[\nA = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\nA = 5000 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.12}{2}\\right)^{2 \\times 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 5000 \\left(1 + 0.06\\right)^{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 5000 \\times (1.06)^2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 5000 \\times 1.1236\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 5618\n\\]\n\nThe amount at maturity is $5618. To find the interest accrued, subtract the principal from the amount at maturity:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Interest} = A - P = 5618 - 5000 = 618\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the interest accrued at maturity is $618.\n\nThe correct answer is **B) $618**."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine the area of the 1-metre-wide boundary around the rectangular plot and then calculate the cost of gardening that area at the given rate. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the given information:**\n   - The perimeter of the rectangular plot is 340 metres.\n   - The boundary to be gardened is 1 metre wide around the plot.\n   - The cost of gardening is 10 per square metre.\n\n2. **Determine the dimensions of the rectangular plot:**\n   - The perimeter \\( P \\) of a rectangle is given by the formula: \n     \\[\n     P = 2 \\times (\\text{length} + \\text{width})\n     \\]\n   - We know \\( P = 340 \\) metres, so:\n     \\[\n     2 \\times (\\text{length} + \\text{width}) = 340\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying, we get:\n     \\[\n     \\text{length} + \\text{width} = 170\n     \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the area of the 1-metre-wide boundary:**\n   - The boundary is 1 metre wide around the entire plot, so it forms a larger rectangle around the original plot.\n   - The dimensions of the larger rectangle are:\n     - Length of the larger rectangle = \\(\\text{length} + 2\\) metres\n     - Width of the larger rectangle = \\(\\text{width} + 2\\) metres\n   - The area of the larger rectangle is:\n     \\[\n     (\\text{length} + 2) \\times (\\text{width} + 2)\n     \\]\n   - The area of the original rectangle is:\n     \\[\n     \\text{length} \\times \\text{width}\n     \\]\n   - The area of the 1-metre-wide boundary is the difference between these two areas:\n     \\[\n     (\\text{length} + 2) \\times (\\text{width} + 2) - \\text{length} \\times \\text{width}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Simplify the expression for the area of the boundary:**\n   - Expanding the expression for the larger rectangle:\n     \\[\n     (\\text{length} + 2) \\times (\\text{width} + 2) = \\text{length} \\times \\text{width} + 2\\text{length} + 2\\text{width} + 4\n     \\]\n   - Subtracting the area of the original rectangle:\n     \\[\n     2\\text{length} + 2\\text{width} + 4\n     \\]\n   - Since \\(\\text{length} + \\text{width} = 170\\), we substitute:\n     \\[\n     2 \\times 170 + 4 = 344\n     \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the cost of gardening:**\n   - The area of the boundary is 344 square metres.\n   - The cost of gardening is 10 per square metre.\n   - Total cost = \\(344 \\times 10 = 3440\\).\n\nTherefore, the cost of gardening the 1-metre-wide boundary is 3440. The correct answer is:\n\nC) 3440"

"To solve this problem, we need to determine how many flowers the bee flies by in order to bypass 8 flowers, given that it bypasses 0.05% of the flowers it encounters.\n\nLet's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the percentage bypassed**: The bee bypasses 0.05% of the flowers it flies by. This means that for every 100 flowers it flies by, it bypasses 0.05 flowers.\n\n2. **Set up the equation**: We need to find the total number of flowers, \\( x \\), that the bee flies by to bypass 8 flowers. The relationship can be expressed as:\n   \\[\n   0.05\\% \\times x = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. **Convert the percentage to a decimal**: \n   \\[\n   0.05\\% = \\frac{0.05}{100} = 0.0005\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute and solve for \\( x \\)**:\n   \\[\n   0.0005 \\times x = 8\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\( x \\)**:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{8}{0.0005} = 16000\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the bee will fly by 16,000 flowers to bypass 8 flowers.\n\nThe correct answer is: **D) 16000**"
'To solve this problem, we need to determine how Fernando can allocate his 3 lunches and 3 dinners during the weekdays, given the constraints.\n\n1. **Lunch Allocation:**\n   - Fernando has 5 weekdays (Monday to Friday) to allocate his 3 lunches.\n   - The number of ways to choose 3 days out of 5 for lunch is given by the combination formula \\( \\binom{5}{3} \\).\n\n   \\[\n   \\binom{5}{3} = \\frac{5 \\times 4 \\times 3}{3 \\times 2 \\times 1} = 10\n   \\]\n\n2. **Dinner Allocation:**\n   - Fernando has 4 weekdays (Monday to Thursday) to allocate his 3 dinners, since he goes home for dinner on Friday.\n   - The number of ways to choose 3 days out of 4 for dinner is given by the combination formula \\( \\binom{4}{3} \\).\n\n   \\[\n   \\binom{4}{3} = \\frac{4 \\times 3 \\times 2}{3 \\times 2 \\times 1} = 4\n   \\]\n\n3. **Total Number of Options:**\n   - The total number of ways to allocate both lunches and dinners is the product of the two combinations calculated above.\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total options} = \\binom{5}{3} \\times \\binom{4}{3} = 10 \\times 4 = 40\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is \\( \\boxed{40} \\).\n\nLooking at the answer choices, the correct choice is:\n- **A) \\( \\binom{5}{3} \\times \\binom{4}{3} \\)**\n\nThus, the answer is option A.'
'To solve the problem, we need to simplify the expression \\(\\frac{a^2 - b^2}{(a + b)^2}\\) and see which of the given options matches the simplified form.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Recognize the Identity:**\n   \\[\n   a^2 - b^2 = (a - b)(a + b)\n   \\]\n   This is a difference of squares identity.\n\n2. **Substitute the Identity:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{a^2 - b^2}{(a + b)^2} = \\frac{(a - b)(a + b)}{(a + b)^2}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Simplify the Expression:**\n   - Cancel out \\((a + b)\\) from the numerator and the denominator:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{(a - b)(a + b)}{(a + b)^2} = \\frac{a - b}{a + b}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Compare with the Given Options:**\n   - We need to find which option matches \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\).\n\n5. **Evaluate the Options:**\n   - A) \\((a + b)(a - b)\\) simplifies to \\(a^2 - b^2\\), which is not equal to \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\).\n   - B) \\((a - b)^2\\) simplifies to \\(a^2 - 2ab + b^2\\), which is not equal to \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\).\n   - C) \\((a + b)^2\\) simplifies to \\(a^2 + 2ab + b^2\\), which is not equal to \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\).\n   - D) \\(a^3 + b^3\\) is not related to \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\).\n   - E) None of these.\n\nSince none of the options match \\(\\frac{a - b}{a + b}\\), the correct answer is:\n\n**E) None of these**'
"To solve the problem, we need to find a number that is equally distant from 36 and 86. This means the number is the midpoint between 36 and 86. Let's follow the steps to find this number:\n\n1. **Identify the two numbers**: 36 and 86.\n\n2. **Calculate the midpoint**: The midpoint of two numbers can be found by taking the average of the two numbers. The formula for the midpoint is:\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Midpoint} = \\frac{\\text{First number} + \\text{Second number}}{2}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Substitute the given numbers into the formula**:\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Midpoint} = \\frac{36 + 86}{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Perform the addition**:\n\n   \\[\n   36 + 86 = 122\n   \\]\n\n5. **Divide the sum by 2 to find the midpoint**:\n\n   \\[\n   \\text{Midpoint} = \\frac{122}{2} = 61\n   \\]\n\n6. **Verify the result**: The number 61 is indeed equally distant from 36 and 86 because:\n\n   - The difference between 61 and 36 is \\(61 - 36 = 25\\).\n   - The difference between 86 and 61 is \\(86 - 61 = 25\\).\n\n   Both differences are equal, confirming that 61 is the correct midpoint.\n\nTherefore, the number that is equally distant from 36 and 86 is 61.\n\nThe correct answer is: **D) 61**."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine how much of the wall A and B can construct together in one minute, and then use that to find out how long it will take them to construct the entire wall together.\n\n1. **Determine the rate of work for A:**\n   - A can construct the wall in 40 minutes.\n   - Therefore, A's rate of work is \\( \\frac{1}{40} \\) of the wall per minute.\n\n2. **Determine the rate of work for B:**\n   - B can construct the wall in 45 minutes.\n   - Therefore, B's rate of work is \\( \\frac{1}{45} \\) of the wall per minute.\n\n3. **Determine the combined rate of work for A and B:**\n   - The combined rate of work when A and B work together is the sum of their individual rates:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{40} + \\frac{1}{45}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Find a common denominator to add the fractions:**\n   - The least common multiple of 40 and 45 is 360.\n   - Convert the fractions to have a common denominator:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1}{40} = \\frac{9}{360}\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1}{45} = \\frac{8}{360}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Add the fractions:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{9}{360} + \\frac{8}{360} = \\frac{17}{360}\n   \\]\n\n6. **Determine the time needed to construct the wall together:**\n   - The combined rate of work is \\( \\frac{17}{360} \\) of the wall per minute.\n   - To construct the entire wall, they need to complete 1 whole wall, so we set up the equation:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{17}{360} \\times \\text{time} = 1\n   \\]\n   - Solving for time gives:\n   \\[\n   \\text{time} = \\frac{360}{17} \\approx 21.18 \\text{ minutes}\n   \\]\n\n7. **Round to the nearest whole number:**\n   - The closest whole number is 21 minutes.\n\nTherefore, the time needed for A and B to construct the wall together is approximately 21 minutes.\n\nThe correct answer is: **D) 21 min**"
"To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes for the entire train to pass through the tunnel. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Train Speed**: The train is traveling at 120 miles per hour.\n\n2. **Tunnel Length**: The tunnel is 1 mile long.\n\n3. **Time to Enter Tunnel**: It takes the train exactly 3 seconds to enter the tunnel. This means that the length of the train is covered in 3 seconds.\n\n4. **Convert Speed to Miles per Second**: \n   - Since the train's speed is given in miles per hour, we need to convert this to miles per second to work with the time in seconds.\n   - There are 3600 seconds in an hour (60 minutes x 60 seconds).\n   - Therefore, the train's speed in miles per second is \\( \\frac{120 \\text{ miles/hour}}{3600 \\text{ seconds/hour}} = \\frac{1}{30} \\text{ miles/second} \\).\n\n5. **Length of the Train**: \n   - Since the train takes 3 seconds to enter the tunnel, and it travels at \\(\\frac{1}{30}\\) miles per second, the length of the train is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Length of train} = 3 \\text{ seconds} \\times \\frac{1}{30} \\text{ miles/second} = \\frac{3}{30} \\text{ miles} = \\frac{1}{10} \\text{ miles}\n   \\]\n\n6. **Total Distance to Pass Through the Tunnel**: \n   - To completely pass through the tunnel, the train must cover its own length plus the length of the tunnel.\n   - Total distance = Length of train + Length of tunnel = \\(\\frac{1}{10} \\text{ miles} + 1 \\text{ mile} = \\frac{11}{10} \\text{ miles}\\).\n\n7. **Time to Pass Through the Tunnel**: \n   - The time it takes to pass through the tunnel is the total distance divided by the speed of the train.\n   - Time = \\(\\frac{11/10 \\text{ miles}}{1/30 \\text{ miles/second}} = \\frac{11}{10} \\times 30 = 33 \\text{ seconds}\\).\n\nTherefore, the train will take 33 seconds to completely pass through the tunnel. The correct answer is:\n\nD) 33 seconds"
"To solve this problem, we need to determine the highest simple interest rate at which the merchant can afford to borrow money to take advantage of the discount. Let's break it down step by step:\n\n1. **Invoice Amount**: $20,000\n\n2. **Discount Terms**: 4/30, n/100\n   - This means a 4% discount is available if the invoice is paid within 30 days. Otherwise, the full amount is due in 100 days.\n\n3. **Discount Amount**: \n   - 4% of $20,000 = 0.04 × $20,000 = $800\n\n4. **Discounted Price**: \n   - $20,000 - $800 = $19,200\n\n5. **Time Period to Take Advantage of the Discount**: \n   - 30 days\n\n6. **Remaining Time to Pay the Full Invoice Amount Without Discount**: \n   - 100 days\n\n7. **Effective Borrowing Period to Take Advantage of the Discount**: \n   - 100 days - 30 days = 70 days\n\n8. **Interest Calculation**:\n   - The merchant needs to determine the highest simple interest rate for borrowing $19,200 for 70 days to save $800.\n\n   - The interest formula is: \n     \\[\n     \\text{Interest} = \\text{Principal} \\times \\text{Rate} \\times \\frac{\\text{Time}}{365}\n     \\]\n\n   - Here, the interest should be equal to the discount amount ($800) to make it worthwhile to borrow the money.\n\n   - So, we set up the equation:\n     \\[\n     800 = 19,200 \\times \\text{Rate} \\times \\frac{70}{365}\n     \\]\n\n   - Solving for the Rate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Rate} = \\frac{800 \\times 365}{19,200 \\times 70}\n     \\]\n\n   - Calculate the Rate:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Rate} = \\frac{292,000}{1,344,000} \\approx 0.21705\n     \\]\n\n   - Convert the rate to a percentage:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Rate} \\approx 21.705\\%\n     \\]\n\nSince none of the answer choices directly match this calculated rate, the correct answer is:\n\nE) None of these"
'To solve this problem, we need to determine how many ways we can distribute 10 lime soda bottles into two groups of 5 bottles each. This is a classic combinatorics problem where we are choosing 5 bottles out of 10 to give to the first group, and the remaining 5 bottles will automatically go to the second group.\n\nHere are the steps to solve the problem:\n\n1. **Understand the Problem**: We have 10 lime soda bottles and need to split them into two groups of 5 bottles each.\n\n2. **Choose 5 Bottles for the First Group**: The number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10 is given by the combination formula:\n   \\[\n   \\binom{10}{5} = \\frac{10!}{5! \\times (10-5)!} = \\frac{10 \\times 9 \\times 8 \\times 7 \\times 6}{5 \\times 4 \\times 3 \\times 2 \\times 1} = 252\n   \\]\n\n3. **Assign the Remaining Bottles to the Second Group**: Once the first group of 5 bottles is chosen, the remaining 5 bottles automatically go to the second group. Therefore, there is no additional calculation needed for the second group.\n\n4. **Conclusion**: The number of ways to distribute the 10 bottles into two groups of 5 is 252.\n\nTherefore, the correct answer is D) 252.'
"To solve this problem, we need to use the given ratio of rice, wheat, and corn in the cereal mixture, which is 2:3:5. This means that for every 2 parts of rice, there are 3 parts of wheat and 5 parts of corn.\n\nLet's break down the steps:\n\n1. **Understand the Ratio**: The ratio 2:3:5 represents the parts of rice, wheat, and corn, respectively. This means that in any given amount of the mixture, for every 2 parts of rice, there are 5 parts of corn.\n\n2. **Determine the Total Parts in the Ratio**: Add up the parts in the ratio to find the total number of parts:\n   \\[\n   2 + 3 + 5 = 10 \\text{ parts}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Find the Weight of One Part**: We know that the bag contains 3 pounds of rice, which corresponds to the 2 parts of rice in the ratio. Therefore, the weight of one part is:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{3 \\text{ pounds}}{2 \\text{ parts}} = 1.5 \\text{ pounds per part}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the Weight of Corn**: Since corn corresponds to 5 parts in the ratio, the weight of corn in the bag is:\n   \\[\n   5 \\text{ parts} \\times 1.5 \\text{ pounds per part} = 7.5 \\text{ pounds}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the bag contains 7.5 pounds of corn.\n\nThe correct answer is: **B) 7.5**"

One soda and two energy bars cost 150 cents:\n   \\[\n   x + 2y = 150\n   \\]\n\n2. Two sodas and three energy bars cost 300 cents:\n   \\[\n   2x + 3y = 300\n   \\]\n\nWe need to solve this system of equations to find the values of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\).\n\n**Step 1: Solve the system of equations**\n\nFirst, let's solve the first equation for \\( x \\):\n\\[\nx = 150 - 2y\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( x \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n2(150 - 2y) + 3y = 300\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( y \\):\n\\[\n300 - 4y + 3y = 300\n\\]\n\\[\n300 - y = 300\n\\]\n\\[\n-y = 0\n\\]\n\\[\ny = 0\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\( y = 0 \\) back into the equation for \\( x \\):\n\\[\nx = 150 - 2(0) = 150\n\\]\n\nSo, the cost of one soda is 150 cents, and the cost of one energy bar is 0 cents.\n\n**Step 2: Calculate the cost of six sodas and seven energy bars**\n\nNow, we need to find the cost of six sodas and seven energy bars:\n\\[\n6x + 7y\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the values of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\):\n\\[\n6(150) + 7(0) = 900 + 0 = 900\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the cost in cents of six sodas and seven energy bars is 900 cents.\n\nThe correct answer is \\(\\boxed{900}\\)."

The correct answer is:\n\nB) Rs. 7.2"
